  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0a45b165-bed5-44fe-84e9-d4ee1c3b9efd'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer12295397767326921701"><i>I know your secret...</i><br/><br/>Stacey's junior year at boarding school isn't easy.   <span id="freeText12295397767326921701" style="display:none"><i>I know your secret...</i><br /><br />Stacey's junior year at boarding school isn't easy. She's not the most popular girl at school, or the smartest, or the prettiest. She's got a crush on her best friend's boyfriend, and an even darker secret that threatens to ruin her friendships for good. And now she's having nightmares again. <br /><br />Not just any nightmares – these dreams are too real to ignore, like she did three years ago. The last time she ignored them, a little girl died. This time they're about Drea, her best friend who's become the target of one seriously psycho stalker. It started with weird e-mails and freaky phone calls. <br /><br />Now someone's leaving Drea white lilies – the same death lilies that have been showing up in Stacey's dreams. Everybody thinks it's just a twisted game . . . until another girl at school is brutally murdered. There are no witnesses. Worst of all, no one has a perfect alibi. With everyone as a potential suspect, Stacey turns to the one secret weapon she can trust – the folk magic taught to her by her grandmother. <br /><br />Will Stacey's magic be strong enough to expose the true killer, or will the killer make her darkest nightmares come true?<br /><br /><b>In this Deluxe Spellbook Edition you'll find:</b><p>Spells created by You and other keepers of secrets-poems, spells and meditations contributed by fans of this popular series. Extras also include an interview with the author.</p></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3402695577?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☠Kayla☠" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☠Kayla☠" href="/user/show/93439193-kayla">☠Kayla☠</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3402695577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18426830225008205776">This book deserves a loose 4 stars. I have to admit while I'm biased of stores that deal with witches and witchcraft I struggled through this one. I found it was a little annoying at times because I couldn't differentiate between dreams and reality. Now I understand that was most likely the point to not know the difference but honestly I found it a little annoying because it seemed to happen all to often then not. I also felt like the characters didn't really have much depth to them and they wer</span>
  <span id="freeText18426830225008205776" style="display:none">This book deserves a loose 4 stars. I have to admit while I'm biased of stores that deal with witches and witchcraft I struggled through this one. I found it was a little annoying at times because I couldn't differentiate between dreams and reality. Now I understand that was most likely the point to not know the difference but honestly I found it a little annoying because it seemed to happen all to often then not. I also felt like the characters didn't really have much depth to them and they were just kind of there. But all in all it was honestly a pretty good book. I admit I loved the spooky atmosphere, the main character was so interesting and I loved her, and the setting was also amazing and, again, a little spooky so that helped persuade my rating. Like I mentioned above I'm biased of witches and witchcraft in books so I did enjoy this read even if it had a few faults. I'd definitely pick up the second book.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_107810471" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107810471" />
    <a title="saguaros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2486548-saguaros"><img alt="saguaros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580937315p2/2486548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107810471?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="saguaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="saguaros" href="/user/show/2486548-saguaros">saguaros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2486548-saguaros?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107810471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11990362316457228048">I think I give it 2.5 stars.<br/>I'm not quite sure about this. I liked it because it was what I needed at the time. Something light and not complicated and silly.<br/><br/>It was like a teen slasher movie with magic, and less dead bodies. But it was so full of cliches and something the writing made me cringe.<br/>I like the main character and I definitely liked the magic in the book. It wasn't too paranormal, just rituals and spells and lots of faith in the magical. Plus, premonition dreams.<br/>So that was fun<br/><br/>Two thin</span>
  <span id="freeText11990362316457228048" style="display:none">I think I give it 2.5 stars.<br />I'm not quite sure about this. I liked it because it was what I needed at the time. Something light and not complicated and silly.<br /><br />It was like a teen slasher movie with magic, and less dead bodies. But it was so full of cliches and something the writing made me cringe.<br />I like the main character and I definitely liked the magic in the book. It wasn't too paranormal, just rituals and spells and lots of faith in the magical. Plus, premonition dreams.<br />So that was fun<br /><br />Two things though.<br /><br />1) Why is it that, often (but not always), in young adult fiction, especially aimed at teenage girls, the "best " fiend(s) are never really good friends. They're always cliche or mean or petty or any other thing that is annoying and that leaves you wondering why the protagonist is their friend to begin with. I haven't read a lot a really strong friendships in young adult books. Especially between girls.<br />And in this book, every single friend that the protagonist had, ended up being annoying, inconsiderate, cold, jealous, mean, or just plain incompatible. <br />My world for a string friendship between two teenage girls where they don't argue about silly things and especially about boys.<br /><br />2) Boys and love interest. Why do they always have to have one? It's like writers and publishers don't think teenage girls can get interested in a book if there isn't some kind of love story going on. <br />Oh, don't get me wrong. I love love stories, and I think that when it's well done, it just enriches the story you are telling, especially if the story is not mainly a love story to begin with. But to make teenage girl characters constantly obsessed with getting a boyfriend, or talking about boys all the time, when your story is not a love story is quite annoying and distract from the story.<br /><br />In this book, I couldn't have cared less about Stacey's feelings for Chad. And her torment, because he was her best friend's ex, who she still thought she loved. And, cue drama, that brings nothing to the main plot line. And Chad didn't seem that much of a catch to begin with.<br /><br />So yeah, 3 stars for the magic in this book. Two for the rest. Because, even though a whole bunch of things annoyed me, I still wanted to keep reding to see how it ended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11990362316457228048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_51637795" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51637795" />
    <a title="Lavanya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1502456-lavanya"><img alt="Lavanya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1224350726p2/1502456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51637795?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lavanya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lavanya" href="/user/show/1502456-lavanya">Lavanya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one in particular</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer51637795&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51637795" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5820014478359138392">I did not like this book very much and I am really surprised the book has avg rating of 4.21 (which is what drove me to read the book in the first place). The book isn't entirely bad though. It is action-packed and has an interesting, yet creepy plot. With that said, I felt like the author placed a greater emphasis on the plot, rather than the characters. I couldn't relate to any of them at all, and felt like many of them didn't have distinct personalities. That bothered me greatly. I won't reco</span>
  <span id="freeText5820014478359138392" style="display:none">I did not like this book very much and I am really surprised the book has avg rating of 4.21 (which is what drove me to read the book in the first place). The book isn't entirely bad though. It is action-packed and has an interesting, yet creepy plot. With that said, I felt like the author placed a greater emphasis on the plot, rather than the characters. I couldn't relate to any of them at all, and felt like many of them didn't have distinct personalities. That bothered me greatly. I won't recommend this book to anyone in particular, unless someone is looking for a quick-read to keep them entertained for an hour or two. The novel is fine, actually, but it's not like Harry Potter or Twilight. I can't get really "into" it. <br /><br />Here come the **spoilers**: This book is about a girl/"witch" named Stacy Brown. She has weird nightmares about her best friend and current roommate, Drea. They seem to foreshadow Drea's death. In these dreams, lilies are all always present; lilies also happen to be the flower that represent death. Stacy becomes really worried because she has had dreams like this in the past, and the last time she didn't act upon them. The result was the death of a little girl named Maura. Stacy isn't sure if she is misinterpreting her nightmares, so she uses card-reading to verify her visions. They all seem to indicate the same thing: Chad, Drea's ex-boyfriend is going to schedule something like date, then cancel on her, Drea is going to get mysterious packages and Drea is going to die soon. To make things even worse, Drea is getting calls from a mysterious guy, and she refuses to tell Stacy who he is.<br /><br />A few days later, Drea gets a package and Stacy becomes paranoid. Stacy doesn't want to tell Drea what her visions indicate, but after these odd phone calls, and the mysterious package, Stacy decides it's about time to tell her the truth. Stacy also tells Amber who is another friend of theirs. Drea doesn't take Stacy's warning seriously. The next day, Drea receives an odd message about Drea having only four more days. Along with the message is four lilies. Drea and Stacy are convinced that the number of lilies represent the number of days Drea has to live. However, despite this, Drea continues to talk to the mysterious guy on the phone, and she admits to Stacy and Amber that she has no idea who he is. Amber completely flips out, and advises her not to talk to him again. <br /><br />Stacy takes it upon herself to solve this mystery, and begins to get threatening messages. A mean girl named Veronica starts telling everyone that she is being stalked too, and has been sentenced to die the same day Drea has; however, Stacy feels that there is more to that story and Veronica is not telling the truth. All of a sudden, Veronica is murdered, which forces the police to get involved. Meanwhile, Stacy has problems with her relationship with Chad. She likes him, and she's pretty sure he likes her, but he was Drea's ex-boyfriend. Drea also gets annoyed with Stacy when she spends time with Chad, and that results in a major fight between Stacy and Drea. On top of all this, Stacy is having nightmares about Chad being the threating person/stalker. The day Veronica dies, Drea hyperventilates and is taken to the hospital. She is released later that night, but she never makes it back to her room. <br /><br />Stacy becomes worried and alerts the police but they aren't too concerned; in their eyes, Veronica's death is the main the problem. Stacy goes searching for Drea, and relies on her visions and her instinct to find her. She goes to a forest (after calling the police and letting them know), and finds Donnovan, a guy who has had a crush/obsession on Drea since third grade, there. Stacy cuts her foot, and Donnovan tells her to stay put while he goes and looks around for some help (apparently his cell phone had no connection). At first she trusts him, but the she questions why he is even here in the first place. That makes her suspicious so she continues her search for Drea. Donnovan gets mad and tells her that she wouldn't want to see what happened to her. <br /><br />Stacy finds Drea in the fetal position all tied up in a shed-like place. The two of them try to escape from Donnovan while he threatens them with a knife. When it almost seems like Stacy is going to die, the police appear on the scene just in time. Donnovan is arrested and taken away, while Drea and Stacy are taken back to the various locations to be questioned by different people.<br /><br />In the end, it turns out that Donnovan was the one who was threatening Drea from the beginning. Donnovan has been obsessed with Drea since third-grade, but she didn't like him back in that sense. Donnovan thought that if he could lure Drea away from Chad and her friends, and spend sometime with her, she would possibly love him. Veronica realized that Drea was getting a lot attention through this problem, and decided to fake the idea of being stalked too. She decided that she would leave town the day of the "murder," and when she came back Drea would be gone, as in dead. With Drea out of the way, she could have Chad to herself. However, Donnovan got upset with Veronica and decided that he had to do something about her. So, as he tells the court, he "accidentally" killed her. The court decides that Donnovan is not mentally straight, and he is sent to juvenile-jail for five years. They also require some counseling sessions for Donnovan. <br /><br />Meanwhile, Drea decides to leave campus and go back home to study for a year. She needs time to get over this ordeal. Also, she thanks Stacy for not bailing out on her, even though she was extremely rude to Stacy. Lastly, she gives permission to Stacy to date Chad.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5820014478359138392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_49550987" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49550987" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosa" href="/user/show/1913711-rosa">Rosa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1913711-rosa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1913711-rosa?shelf=paranormal-fiction">paranormal-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer49550987&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49550987" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11363151478131503625">Stacy starts having nightmares about her friend Drea being kidnapped. She knows that they mean something because this has happened to her before. In the past she ignored them and lost someone she loved because of it. This time Stacy plans on preventing the murder. There were a couple things in this book that struck me as false; it doesn't seem to take place now, it has kind of a mid 90s feel, which is weird. It seems unbelievable that only one student at this wealthy prep school has a cell phone</span>
  <span id="freeText11363151478131503625" style="display:none">Stacy starts having nightmares about her friend Drea being kidnapped. She knows that they mean something because this has happened to her before. In the past she ignored them and lost someone she loved because of it. This time Stacy plans on preventing the murder. There were a couple things in this book that struck me as false; it doesn't seem to take place now, it has kind of a mid 90s feel, which is weird. It seems unbelievable that only one student at this wealthy prep school has a cell phone. Also everyone is catty and bitchy, it seems as though no one is nice to each other, even best friends. I am not saying people have to be nice to each other all the time, but best friends usually have boundaries they wont cross with each other and that doesn't seem to exist here.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6524879-melodramaticfool?shelf=quick-reads">quick-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240725440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11722580079139712672"><b>SEE THIS REVIEW ON MY BLOG!</b><br/><a href='http://melodramaticreviews.blogspot.com/2013/08/blue-is-for-nightmares-by-laurie-faria.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melodramatic Reviews</a><br/><br/>**spoiler alert**<br/>This book was a nightmare! I was seriously tempted for one star.<br/><br/> <br/><br/>A young adult witchcraft book that tries too hard to be adult, in my opinion.<br/><br/>Stacey is a "woe is me" character, whose friends suck. With friends like these, her enemies in the book don't seem so bad anymore! One of them humiliates her in front of her crush out of jealousy. Wow. Not to mention, Stacey's oh-so-wet-dream worthy love interest, was completely unmemorable. S</span>
  <span id="freeText11722580079139712672" style="display:none"><b>SEE THIS REVIEW ON MY BLOG!</b><br><a href="http://melodramaticreviews.blogspot.com/2013/08/blue-is-for-nightmares-by-laurie-faria.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melodramatic Reviews</a><br><br>**spoiler alert**<br>This book was a nightmare! I was seriously tempted for one star.<br><br> <br><br>A young adult witchcraft book that tries too hard to be adult, in my opinion.<br><br>Stacey is a "woe is me" character, whose friends suck. With friends like these, her enemies in the book don't seem so bad anymore! One of them humiliates her in front of her crush out of jealousy. Wow. Not to mention, Stacey's oh-so-wet-dream worthy love interest, was completely unmemorable. So forgettable in fact, that I can't remember his name! Chad? Chase? Conrad? I immediately placed who the villain was and found myself wanting to scream at how dim witted the characters were. I mean this guy screamed creepy!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363959ra/715494.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Stupidity hurts...</i><br><br>I'll give the book kudos for accuracy in their flower language, and the fact that someone actually dies in this book! <br><br>These, ladies and gentlemen, were it's only good points.<br><br>Now. The whole story revolved around a stalker, and the fact that Stacey was having prophetic nightmares. Nightmares that made her wet her bed, but not out of fear! No, no, just because during the dream she had this strong urge to piss herself and couldn't seem to wake herself out of the dream in order to use the toilet like a grown up. Weird and weirder. So we try to grasp the fact that Stacey is trying to hide her bed wetting for nearly the entire book.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363959ra/715495.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>To sum it up, this book was blah. Blah, blah, blah. So blah, I'm not even going to bother reading the other 3 books or the damn graphic novel.</span>

<div id="review_195431103" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195431103" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5977936-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366204418p2/5977936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195431103?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/5977936-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195431103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17495398313468641659">It was such an amazing novel that I really did not want to put it down because I wanted to keep on reading to the end to find out who the stalker was.<br/><br/><br/><br/>Stacey is a wicca who has been having a bed-wetting problem ever since she began to have nightmares about someone trying to kill her best friend and dorm roommate, Drea. When someone starts prank calling their room and leaving creepy notes to Drea, Stacey knows all too well that her dreams are a premonition for a murder...Drea's murder. She, Drea, </span>
  <span id="freeText17495398313468641659" style="display:none">It was such an amazing novel that I really did not want to put it down because I wanted to keep on reading to the end to find out who the stalker was.<br /><br /><br /><br />Stacey is a wicca who has been having a bed-wetting problem ever since she began to have nightmares about someone trying to kill her best friend and dorm roommate, Drea. When someone starts prank calling their room and leaving creepy notes to Drea, Stacey knows all too well that her dreams are a premonition for a murder...Drea's murder. She, Drea, and all her friends must now try to figure out who the stalker is before someone comes and take Drea away before it is too late.<br /><br /><br /><br />I really found all the characters to be quite different and very well written. I felt bad for Stacey's little problem because it kept happening because of those nightmares. I will say that I kinda guessed who the stalker/killer was early on but I wasn't completely sure and I was so intrigued to get to the end to figure out of I was right or not...not alot of mystery books have done that for me.<br /><br /><br /><br />I would definitly recommend this book and series to anyone.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trisha" href="/user/show/1238273-trisha">Trisha</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1901106566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer848488236989519349"><i> "The spirit of dreams is everlasting," I whisper. "It lives within my mind."</i><br/><br/>Light and easy. This one was just okay. I liked the Wicca/Pagan type slant to the story. Stacey was interesting with all her spells and rituals. But<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ I found the bed-wetting part of the story unnecessary......and she doesn't seem all that worried about! I would be scared to sleep, setting alarms to get up all night long to go to the bathroom and go before bed....but she doesn't seem to do any of that <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide</a></span></span>
  <span id="freeText848488236989519349" style="display:none"><i> "The spirit of dreams is everlasting," I whisper. "It lives within my mind."</i><br /><br />Light and easy. This one was just okay. I liked the Wicca/Pagan type slant to the story. Stacey was interesting with all her spells and rituals. But<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I found the bed-wetting part of the story unnecessary......and she doesn't seem all that worried about! I would be scared to sleep, setting alarms to get up all night long to go to the bathroom and go before bed....but she doesn't seem to do any of that <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I also didn't much like most of the cast of characters. Amber and Drea were awful friends. Between sharing secrets with strangers and constantly not trusting or believing each other, I just couldn't imagine these people had been friends for long. <br /><br />The guys were equally rough. Between PJ, Donovan and Chad, I though they ALL were the stalker. None of them were particularly great or even interesting. They were creepy and gross and often lied. <br /><br />Meh. this one was just okay.</span>

<div id="review_513080973" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/513080973" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6369943-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383270274p2/6369943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513080973?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/6369943-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513080973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17285085992540077451">From my blog, <a href='http://averlaine.wordpress.com/2013/01/22/blue-is-for-nightmares-laurie-faria-stolarz/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Writer Diaries</a>.<br/><br/>I didn't like this book. At all. I found myself skipping through paragraphs of description, mostly the spells, cause it felt like a big info dump. You use playing cards because...... insert lengthy reason why. You use oil because...... another lengthy reason why. I feel like I know more about calming oils and protection spells than I do the characters.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380406152ra/792026.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Stacy starts having nightmares about something terrible happening to her friend Drea. She knows that they mean so</span>
  <span id="freeText17285085992540077451" style="display:none">From my blog, <a href="http://averlaine.wordpress.com/2013/01/22/blue-is-for-nightmares-laurie-faria-stolarz/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Writer Diaries</a>.<br><br>I didn't like this book. At all. I found myself skipping through paragraphs of description, mostly the spells, cause it felt like a big info dump. You use playing cards because...... insert lengthy reason why. You use oil because...... another lengthy reason why. I feel like I know more about calming oils and protection spells than I do the characters.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380406152ra/792026.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Stacy starts having nightmares about something terrible happening to her friend Drea. She knows that they mean something because this has happened to her before with a child she babysat, Maura. This time Stacy plans on preventing Drea's death.<br><br>And here I was rooting for Drea to die. She is the worst kind of itch with a heavy case of B. She's a horrible, arrogant friend who believes 'whats mine is mine' including people. She even tells Stacy's crush that she wets her bed - we'll address this little problem later - all because she walked in their dorm and found them sleeping. Fully clothed. A parent would get angry. Your best friend should not, especially since she isn't dating that guy anymore. But alas, Drea thinks he and every other guy in school, belong to her. Honestly, I don't know why Stacy tried so hard to be her friend. I wouldn't want anything to do with her with how she treats people.<br><br>I kept getting the vibe this was set in the 90s, what with all the payphones, and a mention of a walkman. It seems unbelievable that only one student at this wealthy prep school has a cell phone, so I'm going to guess it was 90s.<br><br>Oh, and Stacy is a bedwetter. There's nothing wrong with it, but did the author really have to address it every. single. scene? I couldn't go two pages without Stacy peeing all over herself. Honey, get that checked out. It was explained in the book, but the author doing it over and over again for a total of 9 million times in the book is overdone. I read more about peeing than a plot.<br><br>And character development! Ha! I knew the first time they introduced Donovan he would be the one. His obsession made it obvious. There wasn't any doubt in my mind. No suspense. No characterization. Nada.<br><br>Did I mention that I was rooting for the killer to kill everyone? Because they are all horrible characters.<br><br>On Amazon, it DID say it was for ages 7-10. I'll leave this to the middle schoolers. Once upon a time I enjoyed books regardless of what they lacked.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17285085992540077451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1781091233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1781091233" />
    <a title="Wren " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11442507-wren"><img alt="Wren " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443235719p2/11442507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1781091233?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wren " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren " href="/user/show/11442507-wren">Wren </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=young-adult-general">young-adult-general</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=theme-death">theme-death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=theme-kidnapped">theme-kidnapped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=atmosphere-creepy">atmosphere-creepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=theme-dreams">theme-dreams</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=characters-wiccan">characters-wiccan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=halloween-book-challenge-2016">halloween-book-challenge-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1781091233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6921052788320979764"><br/>This review can also be found at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogspot.ca/2017/04/blue-is-for-nightmares-by-laurie-faria.html'>http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogs...</a><br/><br/> Stacey is a junior at a boarding school, a witch, and has been having nightmares about one of her best friends. In these nightmares, it is undeniable that Drea, her friend, is in trouble, and she soon worries that these dreams may come true when strange gifts and phone calls start arriving.<br/><br/>Stacey uses the magic that her grandmother taught her with hopes to reveal who is behind all of this. But will she be able to unravel t</span>
  <span id="freeText6921052788320979764" style="display:none"><br />This review can also be found at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogspot.ca/2017/04/blue-is-for-nightmares-by-laurie-faria.html">http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogs...</a><br /><br /> Stacey is a junior at a boarding school, a witch, and has been having nightmares about one of her best friends. In these nightmares, it is undeniable that Drea, her friend, is in trouble, and she soon worries that these dreams may come true when strange gifts and phone calls start arriving.<br /><br />Stacey uses the magic that her grandmother taught her with hopes to reveal who is behind all of this. But will she be able to unravel the messages in time?<br /><br />So the first thing I'll say is that this book is rather short, but the length works for the story. I was worried that it might be too short and that the ending could be rushed, but it was paced well and I enjoyed it quite a bit.<br /><br />When I started this book I was expecting more of a paranormal or supernatural mystery, but instead what I got was more of a contemporary story with religious or realistic magic. Stacey wasn't the kind of witch who can summon lightning from her fingertips, rather she uses candle magic and reads cards for divination. <br /><br />I really liked this aspect of the story. Most of the witch or magic books that I come across, especially in the young adult genre or range, are more mystical and based in the witches and warlocks of fairy tales and movies. I was surprised to find that the character actually practice Wicca, because I rarely find Pagans or Neo-Pagans in YA books! <br /><br />The mystery itself, of who was targeting Drea, was suspenseful and interesting but to be honest, it didn't feel very original. I was also somewhat disappointed with the ending and who turned out to be the culprit. Their motive didn't make much sense to me, it seemed slightly over the top for the situation. I thought the villain seemed kind of stupid, actually, for thinking that they could get what they wanted through scaring Drea? I can't say much else with spoiling it. <br /><br />Between this book and Deadly Little Secret, I can say that I definitely enjoy the writing of Laurie Faria Stolarz. I will be looking for her books in the future, however, I won't be absolutely rushing to get the sequels. I feel like while I like her books, I'm not absolutely blown away. <br /><br />I recommend this book to people who want to read a more realistic or diverse portrayal of magic! If you want a YA mystery, you may enjoy this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6921052788320979764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1971085718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1971085718" />
    <a title="Basyirah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62044561-basyirah"><img alt="Basyirah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552299674p2/62044561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1971085718?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Basyirah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Basyirah" href="/user/show/62044561-basyirah">Basyirah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1971085718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8056428011613511696">My initial rating would be 2 star but I changed my mind towards the ending because the suspense kept me on my toes. Personally, I didn't quite enjoy the book because the plot buildup was quite slow and messy in the beginning. It took me a while to understand if Stacey, the MC, was having a nightmare or was it like really happening in real life. I got a little confused, but then it got slightly better.<br/><br/>It's a typical high school nonsense, falling in love with your best friend's on-and-off-and-on a</span>
  <span id="freeText8056428011613511696" style="display:none">My initial rating would be 2 star but I changed my mind towards the ending because the suspense kept me on my toes. Personally, I didn't quite enjoy the book because the plot buildup was quite slow and messy in the beginning. It took me a while to understand if Stacey, the MC, was having a nightmare or was it like really happening in real life. I got a little confused, but then it got slightly better.<br /><br />It's a typical high school nonsense, falling in love with your best friend's on-and-off-and-on again boyfriend, bitching about who's better at picking up boys, etc. And our MC here is the typical Miss I Don't Pick Up Boys But I Hang Out With Cool Girls kind of person. And she's a witch. Hooray. Hey, I dig this kind of story but maybe I'm letting emotional state affects my reading mood right now so yeah..... moving on!<br /><br />So Stacey had been having nightmares about Drea, her bff, getting into troubles and she was very convinced someone's trying to harm Drea. But since Drea's the too cool for school kind of person, so they had several conflicts trying to figure out the nightmares. But then she started to receive "gifts" from a stalker guy and it freaked her out senseless and with the help of their other bff, Amber, they started to link event to event, trynna figure out who the stalker was. <br /><br />I'm just gonna say this straight. I thought Amber's a bitch at first then I realised that Drea's the bigger bitch. Also, if I were Stacey, I'd just walk away from this whole mess because hey I'm just trying to help why you gotta be so rude, you know? Anyway, I'm glad she didn't walk away because the stalker was a goddamned psycho. The ending was quite good but there were some things unexplained... as usual. Not that I expected anything (a lie!)<br /><br />The lovey dovey part of the story was so typical high school stuffs, too. But yeah, just the way I love it. I usually cringe and smile at the same time because I'm a sucker for cute stuffs like that. <br /><br />Guess I'll pick up the second book after all. I hope it gets better but what is life without a little disappointment, right?</span>

<div id="review_319355408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/319355408" />
    <a title="Traci" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2345224-traci"><img alt="Traci" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325915082p2/2345224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/319355408?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Traci" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Traci" href="/user/show/2345224-traci">Traci</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6585454-blue-is-for-nightmares">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2345224-traci?shelf=kindle-library">kindle-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2345224-traci?shelf=books-read-in-2012">books-read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2345224-traci?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2345224-traci?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2345224-traci?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2345224-traci?shelf=witches-and-magic">witches-and-magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319355408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10694569267486596263">This is an enoyable, short mystery novel about a young witch who keeps seeing her best friend and roommate kidnapped in her dreams. She knows that these dreams are really premonitions and decides to do whatever she needs to do in order to stop her friend from dying.<br/><br/>Over the course of the novel, several predictions she make end up coming true: she does a cartomancy reading (like tarot, with regular cards) and everything unfolds the way the reading predicts. <br/><br/>In addition to the witchcraft and the m</span>
  <span id="freeText10694569267486596263" style="display:none">This is an enoyable, short mystery novel about a young witch who keeps seeing her best friend and roommate kidnapped in her dreams. She knows that these dreams are really premonitions and decides to do whatever she needs to do in order to stop her friend from dying.<br /><br />Over the course of the novel, several predictions she make end up coming true: she does a cartomancy reading (like tarot, with regular cards) and everything unfolds the way the reading predicts. <br /><br />In addition to the witchcraft and the mystery that's the central plotline of the novel, there's also a love triangle, if you can call it that--Stacey has some crush on her best friend/roomie's boyfriend/ex-boyfriend, Chad, and he likes her too. Gasp. But Drea's still kind of in love with him and therefore thwarts all the opportunities that Stacey and Chad have to talk.<br /><br />I liked the plot of this book, and the witchcraft contained in it was realistic and believable, but while I liked Stacey, I had to dock the stars for her tendency to be a doormat and her friends' tendencies to be obnoxious and/or bitchy. <br /><br />Seriously, I have no idea why Stacey even bothered to help Drea or why afterward she remained friends with her. Her nightmares caused her to wet the bed, which is a problem she's never had before, and when Drea finds out about this she tells everyone all at once--to be catty, not to get support for her friend--and not once does Drea ever apologize for this. Ever. I can tell you right now that if I peed the bed, and my "best friend" decided to announce that? I'm sorry would be the least she could say.<br /><br />I found Amber, PJ, and Chad to be two-dimensional and somewhat forgettable.<br /><br />That being said, the whodunnit at the end was reasonably well done. The character it ended up being was one that I hadn't dedicated much thought to. it wasn't UNenjoyable by any means but I hate reading books where I hate the main characters. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10694569267486596263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5774543854478623625" style="display:none">Rating: 3.5 out of 5 stars<br />I thought this was a nice story that incorporated mystery and fantasy alike and found that I enjoyed this well enough. That said, there were lots of things that I just really didn't like about this. Primarily, I thought this book was extremely slow paced--I mean really slow. For one thing, the first four chapters were dedicated to one night, that in my opinion, didn't really have a lot going on. Another thing I didn't like about the book was the lack of character development in it. Sure, I think some of the characters were well-written, but others were very shallow and I really didn't see any growth. Lastly, I felt that some of the actions and behaviors seemed forced to fit with the storyline.<br />Overall though, <em>Blue is For Nightmares</em> was well-written and I enjoyed the storyline. Plus, I enjoyed the fact that I couldn't guess the mystery and was kind of surprised by it.</span>

<div id="review_139094740" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139094740" />
    <a title="Jacob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4769041-jacob"><img alt="Jacob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295363748p2/4769041.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139094740?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob" href="/user/show/4769041-jacob">Jacob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4769041-jacob?shelf=yong-adoolt">yong-adoolt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139094740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8193922222427546109">2 stars isn't a bad thing in my book. (no pun!) The beginning is rocky--the narrative is clunky and feels very immature due to moments of heavy-handed exposition and generic teen characterizations. The given circumstances also feel annoyingly familiar: we're at a co-ed boarding school, there are creepy goings-on, and our protagonist--Stacey Brown--is a witch. But Stacey is of the Wicca persuasion, and this is a new sort of character to my reading experience. I found myself both intrigued and vag</span>
  <span id="freeText8193922222427546109" style="display:none">2 stars isn't a bad thing in my book. (no pun!) The beginning is rocky--the narrative is clunky and feels very immature due to moments of heavy-handed exposition and generic teen characterizations. The given circumstances also feel annoyingly familiar: we're at a co-ed boarding school, there are creepy goings-on, and our protagonist--Stacey Brown--is a witch. But Stacey is of the Wicca persuasion, and this is a new sort of character to my reading experience. I found myself both intrigued and vaguely bothered by the fact that Wicca has a solid footing in the real world, and is portrayed as such; while the magic of Harry Potter and other similar tales are very fanciful, Stacey's persona and practice is very normal. What I mean is that she's not waving a wand and making cheese explode or something outrageous; she's got bits of plants that she combines together and she's burning candles and she's asking the Earth to help her see and help her be patient and to help her connect with people. There's no cauldrons, there no big POOF moments, but there is evidence in Stacey's story of her having the strength that she seeks through her spells--the insight and the loyalty and the doggedness that helps her to develop as person. While I've never been interesting in becoming Wiccan, I have always been interested in what it's about; where it's coming from. To be honest, while the first half of the book was boring for me, I enjoyed this depiction quite a bit, because it made me rethink my definition of witchcraft. The great strength of this book is that confidently depicts a normal girl having an empowering kind of trust and interest in the natural powers of nature and humanity. The reason I say I was bothered by this is because of my personal belief in the supernatural. It's real, and there's duality to it--good and evil, real and counterfeit--and, to me, Wicca falls under the counterfeit counter. Still, my point is that I appreciated the different depiction of magic in this book, and that it was a means for personal action instead of a copout/quick fix.<br /><br />About page 150, the narrative seemed suddenly better; it was wittier, the dialogue more quick and smart, the contemplative sections more natural and peaceful, the teenage characters more true and developed. Which is great. By the book's end, I was feeling enough for the characters to be emotionally moved by their efforts for one another, and that, really is all I ask of a book. It must be said, though, that the character of Amber, one of Stacey's school friends, was stealing the show in the first half: she's simultaneously the most generic and yet dynamic character in the book. Her ditzy boy-craziness gives her a clear intention that pumps life into every moment that she has on the page. Stacey's interest as a character in this first half is generated more by her unconventional methodology than in any actual characterization. If the author, Laurie Stolarz, would've/could've asserted the rest of her characters as strongly, the book would've been better (and maybe she DID do better later in this series). But as it is, I was satisfied enough for "Blue Is For Nightmares" to be worth my time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8193922222427546109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_128497695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128497695" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1830075-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487678364p2/1830075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128497695?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/1830075-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128497695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17326332209919076597">Well, I feel a bit schizophrenic, with my extremes of likes and dislikes, but a great many YA reads seem to be either very good or very bad, and the very bad get an extra kick from me when they are blatantly poorly pieced together commercial rubbish based on supposed 'high interest' factors in teen reads.<br/> This book is at least not a knock off of the Twilight series, I guess its got that going for it, but then again there's a lot of rubbish that Twilight can't take the blame for out there. <br/>Both t</span>
  <span id="freeText17326332209919076597" style="display:none">Well, I feel a bit schizophrenic, with my extremes of likes and dislikes, but a great many YA reads seem to be either very good or very bad, and the very bad get an extra kick from me when they are blatantly poorly pieced together commercial rubbish based on supposed 'high interest' factors in teen reads.<br /> This book is at least not a knock off of the Twilight series, I guess its got that going for it, but then again there's a lot of rubbish that Twilight can't take the blame for out there. <br />Both the major characters' friends in this amateurish romp are remarkably unrealistically foolish - they need to be to inject some interest in the unimaginative plot, but Stolarz doesn't seem to understand that she is sacrificing plausibility by creating them like this. Of course, the main character, Stacey is not as stupid as her friends, but it simply beggars belief that she would hang out with two friends who do things as foolhardy as flashing a potentially stalking stranger her tits through a broken window in her friends' room (Amber), or talking about her sex life with a stranger who phoned her by mistake and won't give her his name (Drea). Sometimes this story is just plain tacky, IMHO. <br />Because Amber, in particular, is such an unattractive and idiotic character, Stacey is constantly just tolerating her and silently begging for her to leave whenever she is present, and the reader can't help but wonder why anyone like her would hang out with someone like that. OK, Drea is Stacey's room mate and perhaps they had no choice in the share, but Stacey has no other friends in the story, except boys who have been other of her friends' love interest. Similarly stressful on our willingness to suspend reality is the ostensibly sensible Stacey's spells and practice of Wicca, and even holding a seance. Of course, Stacey also practices the usual poor writer's heroine's dimwittedness in venturing into the woods alone when she thinks she's being stalked, worsened, of course, by the fact that the police officer who she had called to meet her there was distracted by one of Stacey's friends and didn't turn up on time, just to thicken the inert plot.<br /><br />And descriptions like "the library appeared just like it has every other day, like a giant brick harmonica dropped down from outer space" are probably sufficient to demonstrate my point that there is no good writing to rescue the poor plotline and characterisation. <br />All that said, many adolescents are in for a bit of titillation, and the formula of sex and magic will probably net Stolarz a reasonable following. I'm sorry I bought the boxed set of the series for my library.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17326332209919076597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109695351" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10045749785096289707">This is another one I didn't enjoy much. It came as an "extra" in a batch of books I got through eBay. Now I know why they wanted to give it away!<br/><br/>I think the author was trying to write a book similar to a teen horror movie. She kept having the characters say and think things like, "It's like some bad horror movie or something," and "This isn't a slasher movie, it's a prep school," and "Some senior boys are treating this like a cheesy horror movie..." Well, I'd say she succeeded, only not in a go</span>
  <span id="freeText10045749785096289707" style="display:none">This is another one I didn't enjoy much. It came as an "extra" in a batch of books I got through eBay. Now I know why they wanted to give it away!<br /><br />I think the author was trying to write a book similar to a teen horror movie. She kept having the characters say and think things like, "It's like some bad horror movie or something," and "This isn't a slasher movie, it's a prep school," and "Some senior boys are treating this like a cheesy horror movie..." Well, I'd say she succeeded, only not in a good way. This was definitely bad and cheesy. I know as the reader I'm supposed to care about what happens to the characters in the book, but they didn't feel like real people at all. The characters were very flat and unpleasant. I had a hard time feeling any sense of dread for the events that were obviously going to happen.<br /><br />It's probably not fair to this book that I'm also reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2001717.Daphne_du_Maurier" title="Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">Daphne du Maurier's</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12873.Rebecca" title="Rebecca by Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebecca</a> because the comparison between the two is like night and day. Rebecca is wonderfully creepy and mysterious with fleshed-out characters who seem real, including an amazing setting that is almost like another character in the story. I'm going to go listen to the last bit of Rebecca and add this book to my donate stack.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney" href="/user/show/2436229-courtney">Courtney</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65131314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16372154772044331611">Amazon rates this book for Grades 7-10, which I think is quite accurate. As an adult who reads a lot of YA novels, this one just didn't do anything for me. Yes, it had drama, yes, it had suspense, but there was little to no character development. A quick and easy read for middle schoolers for sure.<br/><br/>The story takes place at a boarding school, which we are given absolutely no information on. We are also given no information on any of the characters. The story immediately winds up, fast paced, with </span>
  <span id="freeText16372154772044331611" style="display:none">Amazon rates this book for Grades 7-10, which I think is quite accurate. As an adult who reads a lot of YA novels, this one just didn't do anything for me. Yes, it had drama, yes, it had suspense, but there was little to no character development. A quick and easy read for middle schoolers for sure.<br /><br />The story takes place at a boarding school, which we are given absolutely no information on. We are also given no information on any of the characters. The story immediately winds up, fast paced, with the protagonist's roommate being stalked. I found that I didn't care if she was stalked or saved since I knew nothing about her, except that she was very catty (like all the characters) so was therefore unable to empathize with any of them. <br /><br />Eventhough this book is very much for middle schoolers or young high schoolers, some of the content was entirely too adult. The characters say the F word, along with a cocktail of other expletives, and there is a small snippet about sex. I wouldn't want my 13 year old reading this book (if I had one). </span>
  <a data-text-id="16372154772044331611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73936008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1184967538602012332">Stacey's friend and roommate, Drea, is being stalked by a killer. It's up to Stacey to help Drea survive by using the witchcraft and simple spells her grandmother taught her, from creating a protection jar to pyschic dreams.<br/><br/>The characters in this book were completely wooden and cliche. There was no depth to any of them. I felt as though I was watching a teen slasher movie filled with idiot kids just lining up to be knifed. Drea's reactions are inconsistent and bizarre. One moment Stacey is her b</span>
  <span id="freeText1184967538602012332" style="display:none">Stacey's friend and roommate, Drea, is being stalked by a killer. It's up to Stacey to help Drea survive by using the witchcraft and simple spells her grandmother taught her, from creating a protection jar to pyschic dreams.<br /><br />The characters in this book were completely wooden and cliche. There was no depth to any of them. I felt as though I was watching a teen slasher movie filled with idiot kids just lining up to be knifed. Drea's reactions are inconsistent and bizarre. One moment Stacey is her best friend and the next she's being bitchy for no reason and then disolving into tears because OMG someone wants to kill her but oh wait, no don't do something sensible like call the police. Very annoying. The writing is passable, the plot limps along and the pace is agonizingly slow and tepid. <br /><br />Fans of teen slasher books like RL Stein's may enjoy this book, anyone looking for more substance than that will be disappointed. I had to stop reading after getting halfway through the book, I was just getting too annoyed and had no interest in finishing.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1547740490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1547740490" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13473119-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1547740490?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/13473119-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1547740490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8236671172603568629">Decided to read this while waiting for my car to get a WoF.<br/>Went in just wanting to kill time and was honestly pleasantly surprised. It's not an outrageously ground breaking book but it's definitely one, had I read at the time it was published, I would've loved it with my entire heart.<br/>The teen leads were semi realistic. I say that because I got annoyed by the characters a lot. I thought they were ruthlessly nasty at points, completely fake at others, and over all not very good at decision making.</span>
  <span id="freeText8236671172603568629" style="display:none">Decided to read this while waiting for my car to get a WoF.<br />Went in just wanting to kill time and was honestly pleasantly surprised. It's not an outrageously ground breaking book but it's definitely one, had I read at the time it was published, I would've loved it with my entire heart.<br />The teen leads were semi realistic. I say that because I got annoyed by the characters a lot. I thought they were ruthlessly nasty at points, completely fake at others, and over all not very good at decision making. So, like me when I was their age. The relationships they had with one another weren't really established, there's no massive expository beginning to tell you the inner workings of all these characters you're kind of dropped in the middle of their shit and told to run.<br />Same with the too cool to care 'magic system'. Our lead is/practises Wicca(n) and the author said in an interview that while she did research Wicca, she also asked around for 'everyday magic' that people use, like home remedies etc... to give the magic a more tangible less dues ex machina feeling. And it kinda works, I'm not Wiccan so I can't say how into the representation I am because it's not my opinion that matters in that regard. I did think Laurie did a good job at making it tangible. But aside from its believability, you very rarely get exposition on it. Only in the form of flashback, and it's usually in the background of the actual memory.<br />There's a sprinkling of wish fulfillment in this book with its romance, which feels off in a kind of too easy kind of way. Not because they fall in love immediately, no, you get some of their history and the book doesn't take long to put obstacles in their way. It's because at the end of the day, the obstacles just... step aside? I ain't gonna look a gift horse in the mouth.<br />And the ending, while not as climactic as I would've liked, was still surprising. This book, despite me thinking it was pure fantasy/adventure with maybe a side of romance actually tended more towards the murder mystery/horror fields. Which is wild because I haven't read mystery/horror for years now, this book kind of reminded me why I loved the genres so much. But yeah, the ending wasn't as cathartic as I'd have liked it considering how much constant fretting and humiliation we get secondhand from Stacey (the main character). But in giving catharsis up, it made way for some very realistic consequences re: a shitty justice system.<br />All in all, not bad for a time killer, and super small/easy to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8236671172603568629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2722051024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12624822461624074961">What the hell was this... goddamn travesty.<br/>Really, the only reason I’m giving this book two stars instead of one is because it lowkey gives me Fear Street-esque nostalgia vibes. But Fear Street will always be a million times better than this... experience.<br/>I can’t decide if I can no longer take Young Adult seriously (which I doubt, because I love a whole lot of YA) or if this book in particular just happened to suck, but our lovely little 16 year old MC was absolutely full of cringe, and absolute</span>
  <span id="freeText12624822461624074961" style="display:none">What the hell was this... goddamn travesty.<br />Really, the only reason I’m giving this book two stars instead of one is because it lowkey gives me Fear Street-esque nostalgia vibes. But Fear Street will always be a million times better than this... experience.<br />I can’t decide if I can no longer take Young Adult seriously (which I doubt, because I love a whole lot of YA) or if this book in particular just happened to suck, but our lovely little 16 year old MC was absolutely full of cringe, and absolutely delivered on some truly cringe-worthy quotes.<br />And some of those quotes involve her crush. Exhibit A:<br /> ‪“I motion with a nod at the report beneath his perfectly rounded butt-cheeks, and he slides the thing out, all mangled from sittage. Still, the newly formed butt-indentations in the soft white paper almost make me want to frame it.” —actual paragraph, word-for-word, from actual book that I had to read with my own two eyeballs‬.<br />...<br />Either I’m too fucking asexual to function and people who do experience sexual attraction are fucking weird, or the writing in this book was absolutely god awful. I’m hoping it’s the latter scenario. If it’s the first, and allosexual people actually think shit like that, then... I have absolutely... no words. Absolutely judging the fuck out of all of you.<br />That was by far the worst of the quotes, but the writing in general was just... so bad. Not only did the author spell Stephen King’s name wrong (“Steven King”) but there were just... so many editing mistakes, and most of the characters absolutely sucked. There was a point where the main character, Stacey, got into a fight with her best friend Drea over a boy (yes, the same boy whose ‘butt-cheeks’ she obsesses over), and it was absolutely the most petty thing I’ve ever read.<br />I just.<br />I found this book at Goodwill so thankfully I only spent 99¢ on it. Mediocre as all hell.<br />But hey, it counts toward my reading challenge.</span>

<div id="review_1006824135" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Shazia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4541654-shazia"><img alt="Shazia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539288647p2/4541654.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1006824135?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shazia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shazia" href="/user/show/4541654-shazia">Shazia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4541654-shazia?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1006824135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8495547597383950846">Big sigh. I remember loving this series when I was in high school and have been wanting to reread it again to see if I'd still enjoy it. And, spoiler alert, I did not. I can't tell if this is a sign that I'm a boring adult now or that I just liked bad books when I was a teen, or (most likely) my tastes have changed. It is upsetting that I didn't enjoy the book this time around because the concept of the book is amazing, I mean a teenage witch has dreams that can help her stop her best friend's m</span>
  <span id="freeText8495547597383950846" style="display:none">Big sigh. I remember loving this series when I was in high school and have been wanting to reread it again to see if I'd still enjoy it. And, spoiler alert, I did not. I can't tell if this is a sign that I'm a boring adult now or that I just liked bad books when I was a teen, or (most likely) my tastes have changed. It is upsetting that I didn't enjoy the book this time around because the concept of the book is amazing, I mean a teenage witch has dreams that can help her stop her best friend's murder? Despite not liking the book so much, I still think Stacey is a super cool, badass female character, and I do think it's interesting that she casts "realistic" spells (i.e. no hocus pocus stuff, but more like mixing ingredients while setting intentions). Her relationship with her friends was also great, because as annoying and dramatic as things got, the girls would still choose their friendship despite their disagreements. And her friends still respected and participated in Stacey's witchy traditions even if they didn't fully believe in them. <br /><br />A part of the problem can also be that the book is a bit dated now. Also saying things like "Stacey, you're not like other girls" is so gag inducing. ALSO - I feel like some teen-like stereotypes were overly exaggerated in the book. <br /><br />A bit disappointing that I didn't really appreciate the reread and I don't think I'm going to continue the rest of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8495547597383950846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4sRjtLlkDl05UovAf2RngQL24PQCD9D7tz0IqxSkHF+eZqH9ELLIz3B8XxMWRFTqF5UVTQOpZtxW6FGEr7Ciew==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7deDC7X2RzTUnSt58W8AjhmFUaeuhpwaUBEXlWRAZKyRdUFCHCCBpp2z/6qYTzPlDOakHq8gKj2xxE6631TaiA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5783071385514352751">Laurie Faria Stolarz grew up in Salem, MA, attended Merrimack College, and received an MFA in Creative Writing from Emerson College in Boston. <br/><br/>Laurie Faria Stolarz is an American author of young adult fiction novels, best known for her Blue is for Nightmares series. Her works, which feature teenage protagonists, blend elements found in mystery and romance novels.<br/><br/>Stolarz found sales success with he</span>
  <span id="freeText5783071385514352751" style="display:none">Laurie Faria Stolarz grew up in Salem, MA, attended Merrimack College, and received an MFA in Creative Writing from Emerson College in Boston. <br /><br />Laurie Faria Stolarz is an American author of young adult fiction novels, best known for her Blue is for Nightmares series. Her works, which feature teenage protagonists, blend elements found in mystery and romance novels.<br /><br />Stolarz found sales success with her first novel, Blue is for Nightmares, and followed it up with three more titles in the series, White is for Magic, Silver is for Secrets, and Red is for Remembrance, as well as a companion graphic novel, Black is for Beginnings. Stolarz is also the author of the Touch series (Deadly Little Secret, Deadly Little Lies, Deadly Little Games, Deadly Little Voices, and Deadly Little Lessons), as well as Bleed and Project 17. With more than two million books sold worldwide, Stolarz's titles have been named on various awards list. </span>
